## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task involves predicting mechanical stress as a function of strain and temperature, which is a classical problem in solid mechanics and materials science. The relationship captures how materials deform under load at different temperatures, involving elasticity, plasticity, and thermal softening effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': "Hooke's law (linear elasticity)", 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon', 'scenario': 'Linear elastic regime at constant temperature'}
- {'name': 'Temperature-dependent linear elasticity', 'formula': 'sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon', 'scenario': 'Linear elasticity with temperature-dependent elastic modulus'}
- {'name': 'Power-law hardening (Hollomon)', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1', 'scenario': 'Strain hardening in plastic deformation'}
- {'name': 'Ramberg-Osgood type', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2', 'scenario': 'Combined elastic and plastic strain hardening'}
- {'name': 'Johnson-Cook strength model (simplified)', 'formula': 'sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T)', 'scenario': 'Flow stress with strain hardening and thermal softening'}
- {'name': 'Thermal softening power law', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - T)**c3', 'scenario': 'Strain hardening with power-law thermal softening toward melting point'}
- {'name': 'Exponential thermal softening', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T)', 'scenario': 'Thermally activated softening with strain hardening'}
- {'name': 'Voce hardening law', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon))', 'scenario': 'Saturating stress-strain curve approaching ultimate strength'}
- {'name': 'Voce with thermal dependence', 'formula': 'sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon))', 'scenario': 'Saturating hardening with temperature-dependent saturation stress'}
- {'name': 'Swift hardening law', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2', 'scenario': 'Power-law hardening with pre-strain offset'}
- {'name': 'Ludwik additive hardening', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2', 'scenario': 'Yield stress plus power-law strain hardening'}
- {'name': 'Hyperbolic sine creep law (Garofalo)', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * T * sinh(c1 * epsilon)', 'scenario': 'High-temperature creep and flow behavior'}
- {'name': 'Polynomial stress-strain with temperature', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon * T', 'scenario': 'Quadratic constitutive model with cross-coupling'}
- {'name': 'Arrhenius-type thermal activation in flow stress', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * (1.0 / T))', 'scenario': 'Thermally activated dislocation-mediated plasticity'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening at high temperature → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (Tm - T)**c or exp(-c*T) reducing stress
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or rational epsilon/(epsilon + c) forms
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 + f(epsilon) indicating initial yield before hardening
- Strain-temperature coupling → Product terms epsilon*T or epsilon**c1 * T**c2 capturing interaction effects
- Power-law creep regime → sigma proportional to epsilon_dot**c or equivalently epsilon**c with small exponent at high T
- Concave-up vs concave-down stress-strain → Power exponent c1 > 1 gives concave-up, 0 < c1 < 1 gives concave-down (hardening saturation)
- Melting/phase transition singularity → Terms like (c0 - T)**c1 suggesting divergence or vanishing near critical temperature
- Rate-independent plasticity → Stress depends only on strain magnitude, not explicitly on time derivatives
